Dutch East Indies Government Restricts Beer Imports: Sales of Chinese Beer to be Hit Hard 144

According to Ji Zejin, director of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau,

In order to protect the Javanese liquor industry, the Dutch East Indies government has formulated regulations restricting beer, which came into effect on December 13, 1932. The main points of the regulations are three: (1) Importers who imported beer before 1932 can continue to import, and the amount of imports is based on the amount imported in 1931 and 1932; (2) Those who want to import beer must be approved by the Minister of Agriculture, Industry and Commerce; (3) Beer importers must notify the Ministry of Agriculture, Industry and Commerce by telegraph before December 20, and send all previous import documents by January 3 of the 23rd year for verification. Since the implementation of the restriction regulations, beer imports have decreased, and Javanese wine sales have gradually increased. Most of the beer shipped from China is Wuwu beer, and sales are also good in the Chinese community. However, the agent's capital is thin, and it only has three or four years of history, which is inferior to Japanese wine. Recently, it has been restricted by the restriction regulations, and Javanese wine sales have been strong. In addition, the Japanese-established winery in Java has been successful, so the sales of Chinese beer will be severely hit due to the price difference.

A New "East Asia Gold and Silver Night Market Agency" Discovered in This City: Opened on Avenue Joffre Yesterday: Business Starts at 9 PM 146

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the "East Asia Goods Gold and Silver Night Market Agency," newly established by American jockey V. M. Haimovitieh at 989 Avenue Joffre, next to the Weida Hotel, specializes in bidding on gold and silver prices, as well as trading in American wheat, cotton, rubber, and various stocks. It officially opened last night. The general financial circles in this city are mostly unclear about the nature and content of this type of organization and suspect that it is a disguised exchange. Therefore, Tao Xiaoyuan and Chao Hanqing, brokers of the Goods Exchange, and others have hired lawyers Chao Kun and Chao Jimei to send a five-point letter of inquiry, requesting an immediate response. A reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency has made a special investigation and recorded the details as follows:

A Glimpse of the Night Market: The office has only one and a half storefronts along the street. Although it is elegantly decorated, the market is small and can only accommodate a dozen or so customers at most. Compared with the large-scale organization of an exchange, it is very different. Its business hours are from 9 pm to 1 am. The scope of business is very broad, such as bidding on gold, silver, rubber, stocks, American cotton, wheat, etc., all of which can be bought and sold at the office. It already has the scale of a budding commodity and gold exchange, but the content and nature are far inferior.

Business Characteristics: The manager of the office is the American V. M. Haimovitieh, a well-known jockey in Shanghai. Its business nature has very special characteristics: (1) The American longitude and latitude are just the opposite of China's. The day and night in China are in the opposite position to the United States. The office's business hours are set in the evening, which is when business is booming in the United States. Transactions and trades between the East and West, and telegram exchanges, can be reached in just 19 minutes. Foreign exchange between the two sides can be entered and exited at that time, without having to wait until the next day for the transaction to be completed. This type of organization is very unique for American foreign exchange; (2) In ordinary exchange trading, one-tenth of the margin must be paid. The office only requires proof of bank deposits to replace the margin, without the need to prepare additional cash to deposit in the exchange. Therefore, the nature of its organization is really questionable. Tao Xiaoyuan and others have already sent letters of inquiry and have also submitted requests to the authorities for investigation. There should be a fair solution, it is said.

Yuxing Wheel Collides with Civil Ship: Loss of Ship and Cargo Valued at 2,000 Yuan: The Boatman's Wife Cannot Be Rescued 147

The Yuxing Wheel of the Zhaoxing Company in this city entered the port yesterday and collided with a rice boat when it reached Lujiazui. The rice boat immediately sank, and the hull and cargo were all submerged. The details are recorded as follows:

Rice Boat Collided: The Yuxing Wheel of the Zhaoxing Company came to Shanghai from Xinghua, Fujian this time. At 2 p.m. on the 7th, the Yuxing Wheel sailed into the Wusongkou and reached the Huangpu River. When it was about to reach the Longmao Wharf at Lujiazui, a civil ship loaded with rice and grain suddenly came from south to north. The owner of the Yuxing Wheel hurriedly sounded the whistle to order the rice boat to quickly give way and stop. The boatman of the civil ship continued to move forward. The Yuxing Wheel could not stop in time, and the rice boat crashed head-on into the bow of the Yuxing Wheel, immediately capsizing into the river.

Cargo Lost: After the rice boat was hit, the boatman and others all fell into the water, and the cargo in the boat was also lost. Fortunately, the wharf ferry boats of Longmao Wharf and others came forward to help rescue them, and quickly rescued the boatman and others who fell into the water one by one. However, all the cargo in the boat was lost.

Report to Customs: After the incident, the Yuxing Wheel reported the situation to the company and the Customs Port Affairs Department after the ship was berthed. The boatman of the civil ship that was hit and sunk also reported to the Water Patrol Team. Negotiations for Compensation: The Shanghai North Rice Merchants Association Lianyi has sent a letter to the Zhaoxing Company to negotiate compensation. At about 2 p.m. on the 7th, when he arrived opposite the new customs of the Huangpu River, near the patrol boat of the Lujiazui Water Patrol Police Station, Shao's boat was sailing close to the Pudong bank. Suddenly, the Yuxing Wheel of the Zhaoxing Company, which was sailing from north to south along the west bank from the Waibaidu Bridge to the Tongren Wharf, suddenly turned its head and drove straight towards Pudong, without sounding the whistle, and rammed Shao's boat head-on, smashing the boat into two pieces. In addition to Shao himself, there was also Shao's wife, Ms. Qian, 28 years old, and a ten-year-old daughter, as well as a partner named Li Difa, all of whom fell into the water. At that time, the wheel not only did not stop, but also did not rescue them. Fortunately, the water patrol boat was nearby and immediately released the wheel to rescue them. Shao, his daughter, and his partner were rescued, but Shao's wife, Ms. Qian, could not be rescued and must have drowned. In addition to the rear half of the boat that was still floating, the rest was submerged without a trace. The total loss of the boat and cargo is valued at about 2,000 yuan, and his wife, Ms. Qian, was tragically drowned, requesting assistance to negotiate. According to this, the case involves loss of life and loss of ship and cargo, and the circumstances are serious. Based on the facts, the Yuxing Wheel should be fully responsible. Accordingly, we will first inquire with your company about the consolation of the deceased and the issue of compensation, so that we can handle it according to the law. Sincerely, Zhaoxing Wheel Company, Water Patrol Police Station, River Patrol and River Affairs Envoy."

Executive Yuan Strictly Prohibits: Antique Dealers from Smuggling Antiques for Export; Digging Up Ancient Tombs is Prohibited; Preservation Agencies are Established 149

Private digging up of ancient tombs violates the ban. The Ministry of Interior has previously issued a notice to local county governments to strictly prohibit it. However, in recent years, antiquities have been discovered in various provinces and cities. After examining the origin of these antiquities, they were either discovered in cellars or dug out of ancient tombs. Antique dealers in various places often sell them to foreigners because they are greedy for profit. The number of antiques smuggled out of the country every year is very large, and Shanghai is the central area of the antique market. Therefore, in order to preserve the relics of the ancestors, the Executive Yuan has decided to establish a Central Antiquities Preservation Committee. In the future, competent authorities will also be established in various provinces and cities, and talented people with rich knowledge will be hired to specialize in research. On the one hand, the Executive Yuan will issue a notice to all provinces and cities to strictly prohibit the excavation of ancient tombs and decide on methods to preserve antiquities, so as not to flow abroad. Academic groups such as the Geological Survey of the Academia Sinica and the Peiping Research Institute should organize the relics of the ancestors for the purpose of scientific work, including the discovered objects of ancient tombs, in accordance with Article 8 of the Antiquities Preservation Law; (2) Antiquities discovered due to natural damage and construction projects should be handled in accordance with Article 7. The Shanghai Municipal Government is also ordered to strictly prohibit antique dealers from excavating ancient tombs and smuggling antiques for export. If discovered, they should be severely punished, it is said.

Gu Li Shuyun Counter-Sues: Gu Renfa for False Accusation: The Bigamy Portion Will Be Sued After the End of This Case: Wuxi Court Scheduled to Hear the Case on the 12th of This Month: Gu's Whereabouts are Secret, Summons Delivered to the Nanjing Court for Transfer: 丨If Gu Fails to Appear Again, Li Will Request an Arrest Warrant丨 150

Gu Renfa, the former director of the Jiangsu Department of Civil Affairs, transferred Liu Zhuomin, the second branch of the Wuxi Public Security Bureau, despite resistance. Gu accused his wife, Gu Li Shuyun, of being suspected of instigating the matter. At the same time, he also reported to the court that Li had sold official positions. He also dispatched his subordinates to Shanghai to arrest Li Shuyun and her daughter and send them to Wuxi. They were detained in the Wuxi Court. At that time, Li was very angry because she was suddenly wronged. Later, Gu was summoned by the Wuxi Court to question Liu Zhuomin and learned the inside story. He was then allowed to be released on bail by Li's proxy lawyer, Chao Kun, to seek medical treatment in Shanghai. At the same time, Li hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Xiang Xun to jointly sue Gu Renfa for false accusation and accuse Gu of bigamy, together with lawyer Chao Kun. At that time, Gu was asking people to mediate, so Li temporarily did not file the lawsuit. The details were recorded in this newspaper. It is now known that although the case was mediated by someone, Gu had very little sincerity, so there has been no result so far. Therefore, Li formally filed a counter-suit for false accusation with the Wuxi Court on the 4th of this month. As for the bigamy portion, it is planned to file another lawsuit after the end of the false accusation portion. It is now known that the petition has been approved by the court and the court hearing has been scheduled to be held at 2 p.m. on the 12th of this month in the Wuxi Court. At that time, Li Shuyun will go to Wuxi in person to appear in court for confrontation. However, it is known that Gu Renfa has not returned to Shanghai since going to Jiangxi. It is also rumored that Gu has left Jiangxi and gone to Wuhan, so although the Wuxi Court has issued a summons to summon Gu to appear in court at that time, the summons could not be delivered because Gu's whereabouts were secret. However, it has been found that Gu's previous address was in Santiao Lane, Nanjing, so it has been handed over to the Jiangning Local Court for transfer. At the same time, according to Li's side, if Gu fails to appear again, they will request the Wuxi Court to issue an arrest warrant when necessary.

Does the Owner Assume Responsibility for the Through Freight Transportation Method? Whether or Not Escorts Are Needed Depends on the Nature of the Goods; The Railway Department's Through Transportation Office Sent a Letter to the Two Railway Bureaus Yesterday to Comply 154

The Two Railway Bureaus received a letter from the Through Transportation Office yesterday, saying, "Approved the telegram from the Longhai Railway Car Affairs Office stating that on the 9th of this month, two cars of gasoline, No. 6066 and No. 4951, were shipped from Rihui Port in Xuzhou to Tongguan, with freight tickets No. 9244 and No. 0344. The stationmaster of Xuzhou Station of this railway telegraphed Jinpu and Jinghu after seeing that there were no escorts to take care of the goods, and then telegraphed to request accommodation, etc. In order to avoid wasting vehicles, this railway specially approved the receipt of the goods. However, in the future, should the through freight goods for which the owner is responsible be accepted if there are no escorts to accompany them? If an accident occurs in transit after acceptance, how should it be handled? I hope for instructions, etc." After arriving at the office, it was found that whether or not the through freight goods for which the owner is responsible need to be escorted depends on the nature of the goods. For example, live poultry and livestock, explosives, flammable liquids, gold and silver, and other valuables, as well as coal and other items, should be watched at all times to avoid damage or theft. When requesting through transportation, inquiries must be made in advance, and tickets can only be issued if there are escorts. As for other ordinary goods for which transportation is not responsible, such as earth and stone, etc., which are not easily stolen, if the owner can trust the railway and does not send escorts, the through transportation routes may allocate and receive the goods to facilitate business and benefit merchants. The previous reasons for the telegram have been approved. In addition to sending separate letters to each route, a corresponding letter is sent to request compliance." The bureau has already instructed the Car Affairs Office to comply.

Qian Qikun Committed Suicide by Drowning Himself in Paotai Bay; The Reason for the Suicide Can Be Deduced from His Belongings 158

At about 5 pm on the 7th, a young man of about 20 years old went to the beach in front of the Fuzhi Western Restaurant in Wusong Paotai Bay and jumped into the sea to commit suicide. It was dusk, and the tourists on the beach had dispersed. Only a villager caught a glimpse of him and tried to rush to his rescue, but he had disappeared. So he rushed to report to the 2nd detachment of the 7th district. The police chief immediately rushed to the beach to investigate. On the beach, he found the belongings left by the suicide victim and took them to the 7th District Public Security Bureau. After inspecting them, Director Yao found a dog racing magazine, a business card with the words "Gongji Kitchen, Lane 305, Dabu Street, Xinkaihe Road, Republic Road", and a piece of Western paper with two suicide notes written in red ink, one to his parents and one to his sister and brothers. The text had many typos. The original letter is copied as follows (not changing a single character): "Dear parents, these are my last few words. Although I have spent this little money this time, it is very difficult to raise funds in this economic downturn. So I spent a whole day yesterday without any results. I want to make a big mistake, and I have no face to see you again, and my reputation is spreading. Therefore, I will commit suicide to serve as the guest of the River God. The kindness of raising me will be repaid in the next life. Please don't take it to heart, otherwise, I will not be able to rest in peace underground. I wish you good health and a long life. Underneath, Qian Qikun's last words." "To my sisters and brothers, you must treat your parents well and persuade them on my behalf. It is not in vain to be compatriots. Thousands of words, I want to say but can't finish. Take care of yourselves. Qikun." According to this, the reason for his suicide can also be imagined from his belongings.

Drug Manufacturer Xia Jisheng Convicted; Sentenced to One Year and Two Months in Prison and a Fine of 1,000 Yuan 159

On October 5th of last year, French police detectives arrested Wang Zhihao, who was carrying red pills, on Republic Road, and subsequently uncovered the private red pill manufacturing operation at No. 9 Airlike Road. At that time, the boss Xia Jisheng (nicknamed Little Shaoxing, originally in the car business, and formerly an honorary detective in the French Concession) escaped from the roof, and only the two partners Yuan Shunzi and Fan Jin were caught. Red pills and equipment and raw materials were seized and sent to the Second Special Court. After interrogation, Yuan and Fan were each sentenced to six months in prison and fined 500 yuan, and Wang was sentenced to two months in prison and fined 300 yuan. At the same time, the police station requested the court to issue a warrant for the arrest of Xia Jisheng for interrogation. However, Xia hid outside until recently when he sneaked home and was discovered by French police detective Guo Shaorong. On the 21st of last month at 5 pm, Xia was arrested and sent to the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. After Judge Li Changnian repeatedly opened court sessions for interrogation, Xia cunningly refused to admit it and hired Wang Shizong as his lawyer for defense. After the previous case files were retrieved and the two convicts Yuan and Fan were brought to court for confrontation with Xia, the trial was declared closed. Yesterday was the day of sentencing. The police escorted Xia to the court at 10:30 am. Judge Li presided over the first criminal court and sentenced Xia Jisheng to one year and two months in prison for manufacturing opium substitutes, and fined him 1,000 yuan. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. The number of days of detention before the judgment is determined will be deducted from the prison term at the rate of two days for one day. The defendant was allowed to pay a bail of 5,000 yuan secured by three consecutive shops during the appeal period. Xia was taken into custody without bail pending instructions after the sentencing.

A Major Innovation in the Yu-Style Chinese Typewriter 162

Since its invention, the Yu-style Chinese typewriter has been very popular among Chinese people. Its exquisite structure and convenient operation are not only unmatched by similar domestic products, but also difficult for products made and sold by speculators from various countries to compete with, and have been successively eliminated. In recent years, the inventor Yu Binqi, in view of the increasing number of counterfeit typewriters on the market, in order to protect business and increase public confidence, applied to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government for rewards in accordance with the law and was approved for a patent. After passing the review, he was given excellent comments and granted a special patent. After receiving the approval, Yu established a wholly-owned manufacturing factory at No. 541 Zhaofeng Road, and jointly operated with Shanghai Daming, Xie Da, Jing Da, Lu Guiji Longchang, Qiming, and other major famous factories, in order to speed up production and strive for excellence. It is said that after this major innovation, it has been deeply appreciated by social celebrities. In recent days, visitors to the factory have been constantly coming. There is fog and southeast wind along the coast south of Ma'an Island. A low-pressure area and low center point are forming in Jiangxi. Also, within the 24 hours prior to 3:00 PM yesterday, the local temperature reached a high of 70.7 and a low of 68.7. On the same day last year, the high was 81.0 and the low was 62.4.

Acknowledgement: Acknowledgment is made to the Information Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council for the generous gift of a Chinese copy of the "Republic of China 22nd Annual Report," and to the Bank Weekly for the generous gift of the 848th issue of the Bank Weekly. Thank you.

Special Report: Overview of the Work of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration in the First Quarter of the 23rd Year (5) 171

(5) Refurbishing equipment, manufacturing trains for through service to Beijing, renovating carriages, improving passenger car facilities, vehicle standard meeting, expanding track and engineering equipment, dredging docks and harbor channels.

Manufacturing Trains for Through Service to Beijing 172

Since the commencement of through train service between Shanghai and Beijing, this railway was supposed to prepare a passenger train. However, due to the lack of one lounge car, one dining car, and two second-class sleeping cars, they have not yet been added. The Wusong Machine Factory was urged to expedite manufacturing, while the vehicles scheduled for allocation were extensively renovated. The project was completed and test-run on February 20th. The train consists of one first-class sleeping car, one first-class lounge car, two second-class sleeping cars, one dining car, three third-class passenger cars, one guard's car, one heating and postal car, and can accommodate 384 passengers, with 52 sleeper berths. The dining car can accommodate 36 people dining simultaneously. The total cost of renovation and manufacturing reached 177,000 yuan. On the 22nd, the train was parked at the Shanghai North Station to invite people from all walks of life to visit. As the Bureau was then engaged in formulating passenger car standards, and this through train had not yet been manufactured according to the standards, it was naturally not completely satisfactory. This was a good opportunity to solicit criticism from all parties, so as to serve as a reference for determining passenger car standards in the future. The actual operation started on the 25th, and the order of the train was revised after considering and adapting to needs.

Renovating Carriages 173

Regarding the renovation of other passenger cars, during this quarter, two third-class passenger cars with straight seating were converted into transverse seating, fifteen 25-ton wooden tarpaulin cars were converted into steel tarpaulin cars, and two third-class baggage-brakeman cars were converted into heating-baggage-mail-brakeman cars.

Improving Passenger Car Facilities 174

As for passenger car facilities, on the one hand, it concerns appearances, and on the other hand, it is related to passenger comfort. In addition to actively discussing standards, the following treatment measures were also introduced: (1) Repaint all cars with old colors, and ensure the color of each train is consistent, whether new or old, light or dark. (2) The air in the cars must be kept clean, so there should be adequate ventilation equipment. Third and fourth-class cars are crowded, so equipment should be installed as soon as possible for those that lack it. (3) The toilet facilities in all classes of passenger cars should uniformly use porcelain. (4) The lighting in the cars should be sufficient. The lighting in third and fourth-class cars is too dim and should be increased. (5) The heating in third and fourth-class cars in winter should be similar to that in first-class cars. (6) Clothing hooks, etc., should be installed in cars where they are lacking. (7) Third and fourth-class cars have a large number of passengers, so fans should be installed in summer to improve hygiene. (8) The dining car kitchen should be equipped with electric ventilators to prevent odors from spreading. Because the railway's operating income is mainly derived from third and fourth-class passenger transportation, special attention should be paid to the treatment of third and fourth-class passengers. Therefore, the Mechanical and Rolling Stock Department and the Traffic Department were ordered to complete the above-mentioned improvements as soon as possible to benefit travelers.

Vehicle Standard Meeting 175

Regarding the determination of standards for each class of passenger car, the relevant personnel were convened during this quarter to hold a vehicle standard meeting. In addition to adopting reversible seat backs for first-class passenger cars and attaching dining cars to passenger trains (except for local trains) as a principle, and using domestic goods as a principle for materials, a comprehensive opinion on improving equipment was also proposed and is currently under strict review.

Expanding Track Engineering 176

The new projects completed during this quarter include the northern end of the marshalling yard connecting the Nanjing Riverside Station and the Nanjing Qi Station, with a total length of 565 meters, and the connecting line between this track and the first side track of the Capital Railway Ferry, with a total length of 264 meters, for use by the ferry station and locomotives for shunting. In addition, a storage shed was added to Shanghai North Station to accommodate the Beijing-Shanghai through train. The projects under construction include the addition of shunting tracks at the Nanxiang Station, Qiaotouzhen Station, and Hepingmen Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, and at the Nanxingqiao Station and Jianqiao Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. Earthwork is currently being laid, and the required steel rails are also being purchased. To prevent traffic accidents, warning signs prohibiting villagers from crossing the track have already been posted along the line. Recently, 500 new warning signs prohibiting cattle and carts from entering the railway area have been produced, with drawings of cattle and carts to make them more eye-catching. They are being distributed by the Engineering Department to various sections for hanging, including 150 each for the Jingdan and Dansong sections of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, 100 for the Shanghai-Hangzhou section, 20 for the Cao-Ningbo section, and the remaining 80 for future additions and replacements. Dredging Docks and Harbor Channels

In addition, to facilitate cargo lighterage, the coal docks at Nanjing Riverside and the waterways near the Zhenjiang docks, which have shown signs of silting, were deepened. The former was contracted by Gao Yu Ji, with a labor cost of one yuan and forty cents per 2.8317 cubic meters (i.e., one cubic foot). The latter was contracted by Wang Rong Ji at three jiao per cubic meter. Later, Wang Rong Ji applied to withdraw the bid, and it was reassigned to the second-highest bidder, Zhenli Construction Company, which is currently carrying out the work.

(6) Training police officers, admonishing passenger car service employees, training attendants on trains.

Continuing to Recruit Police Recruits 177

Railway police serve the railway and should have appropriate training and knowledge. Therefore, the Bureau has established a police training institute to train them independently. The fourth class of police recruits graduated last year and were assigned to various departments to serve. However, the railway line is very long and difficult to defend. To strengthen the police force, the Bureau, together with the Railway Police Administration, requested and obtained approval from the Ministry of Railways to continue recruiting 60 police recruits for the fifth class and to fill the remaining 11 vacancies from the fourth class, for a total of 71 recruits. Examinations were held at the Nanjing Zhakou on February 21st. If the quota is met, classes will begin on the 26th.

Admonishing Passenger Car Service Employees 178

Railway operations are based on passengers and merchants. As far as this railway is concerned, passenger transport is even more important than freight transport. Therefore, the behavior of service personnel on passenger trains deserves attention. Therefore, a book of admonitions was printed and distributed, listing four major requirements for service: (1) Maintaining cleanliness; (2) Obeying discipline; (3) Treating guests with courtesy; (4) Disciplining oneself strictly, and providing detailed items to follow.

Training Attendants on Trains 179

As for the attendants in sleeping cars, dining cars, and official cars, they are generally poorly educated. If their character is bad, it is difficult to manage them, and dereliction of duty and slow service to guests will follow. Therefore, training methods have been established. First, when selecting them, attention should be paid to whether their physique is strong and lively and whether their responses are fluent and refined. After selection, it is stipulated that each group of attendants should be rotated to the Traffic Department office on their rest days for training. The subjects are mainly civic morality, hygiene knowledge, and service details. When inspectors board the train for inspection, they also provide individual guidance and conduct examinations. If they do not fully understand the items taught, they are explained in detail. At the same time, strict attention is paid to the matters that attendants should pay attention to when serving on the train. Those who violate the regulations will be punished immediately, so as to cultivate their good character and become excellent public service personnel.

(7) Repaying debts, increasing the reserve ratio, repaying advances for purchasing vehicles, repaying Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway debts.

Increasing the Reserve Ratio 180

The Bureau's repayment of the Sino-British Bank debt is made by setting aside a special reserve from the daily operating income to meet the payment. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway's set aside percentage has been gradually increased to 20%. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway originally set aside 5%. From October 1st of last year, it was increased to 7.5%. From January 1st of this year, it was increased to 10%. The two railways set aside a total of approximately 200,000 yuan per month.

Repaying Advances for Purchasing Vehicles 181

The first and second installments of the principal of the advance for purchasing vehicles borrowed by the Beijing-Shanghai Railway from the Sino-British Bank have been repaid last year. The third installment of the principal of £9,000, which was due in January of this year, was repaid in half in February, amounting to 65,954.20 yuan in national currency. The remaining half was repaid in March, amounting to 65,207.55 yuan in national currency. The total amount of 131,161.75 yuan was withdrawn from the above-mentioned special reserve.

Repaying Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Debts 182

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway's debt to the Sino-British Bank has been repaid in 30 installments. The 31st installment of the principal, which was due in November of last year, including bank commissions, totaled £37,593 and 15 shillings. Part of it, £19,500, was repaid in February of this year, amounting to 286,896.55 yuan in national currency. In addition to the 167,500 yuan allocated by the Ministry of Railways, the remainder was also withdrawn from the reserve.

In total, 418,058.30 yuan in Sino-British Bank debts were repaid this quarter. (To be continued)

Reading and Answering Questions: Answering the Questions of Readers after Reading "The Quarterly Journal of Labor Problems" 183

To the questioning reporter:

When I read the advertisement for the Labor Quarterly in Shen Bao, I thought of buying a copy for the library. After reading the questions and answers on April 29th and 30th, I mustered the courage to spend five jiao on postage. After the book arrived, I read it all at once. I couldn't help but write down some opinions and ask for guidance.

The content of the publication, as Mr. Wang said, is only a relatively progressive publication discussing labor issues. There are many imperfections, which cannot be listed in detail here. However, reading Mr. Wang's questions, it seems that he is pointing out the contradiction between the previous and later claims of the publication, as if what was right before is wrong later, and what is right later is wrong before. The two must be one or the other. My opinion is slightly different. To put it bluntly, both are right. Simply because the author of the article "A Review and Significance of the Shanghai Workers' Movement" wrote in a clumsy style, which may have caused Mr. Wang's doubts and the criticism of Mr. and someone else. Please elaborate.

It is an iron law that the national bourgeoisie in colonies and semi-colonies has compradore characteristics. These national capitalists are raised by imperialists and exploited by them at the same time. They can only try their best to compensate from the laboring masses of their own country to protect themselves. This point has been made very clear by Mr. citing the example of India.

However, what kind of attitude should the laboring masses in semi-colonies take towards their own national capitalists? Especially in China, which is backward and needs to move towards state capitalism in a period of transition, what is the most reasonable way to do it?

I would like to raise this question to Mr. for an answer.

I believe that what Mr. Liyan said, "The national labor-capital struggle is often 'more intense than' the ordinary labor-capital struggle," does not "hide" the meaning that "workers would rather be family slaves," but is a conclusion drawn from the facts of the "May 30th" incident and other facts. The reason why it is more intense is precisely because it has economic and political "duality." How can there be the slightest meaning of "wanting to eliminate the workers' rebellious emotions in beautiful words and then abolish the national revolution"? Looking at Mr. Liyan's full text again, it only shows that Chinese workers, especially Shanghai workers, are standing on the front line of anti-imperialism, so there is a conclusion of "main force." According to Mr.'s meaning, the workers are "extremely insufficient," who is enough? Warlords? Intellectuals? National capitalists? Backward peasants?

As for the fifth item of the conclusion, the first half already contains many things "implied beyond words." "And..." Below, in terms of writing, it is a big mistake. However, in a semi-colony with backward industries, the working masses have not yet concentrated into a revolutionary period that can erupt victoriously. The result of the recession only makes some factories close and thousands of workers are laid off. We are just enough to know from the little information contained in the publication! Are the yarn mills in Tianjin, Shanghai, Zhengzhou, Hankou, and Nantong, and the silk mills and silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang all real evidence? Was the outbreak of the Shanghai silk factory strike last year the result of a more severe recession? Or was it a stimulus from the improvement of the silk industry? When all the silk factories stopped at the end of last year and the workers were waiting at home, could a major strike occur? Is this a "brilliant theory"? Or is it a fact? Don't be a prisoner of formal logic!

It is true that the "January 28th" incident stimulated the revolutionary emotions of the workers. However, on the one hand, many factories closed down or were destroyed by artillery fire, and the workers were displaced, leading to a decline in the labor movement. This is at least one aspect of the fact! Of course, the workers' inner anger has risen. However, as in Russia after the 1905-1907 revolution, was the temporary decline of the workers' movement not also a fact? Moreover, the author did not say that this was the only reason! This article has problems. Clumsy writing is one of them, and some of it may be to avoid something.

I have written hundreds of words above in a jumble, and I respectfully ask for corrections.

Liu Zili, Zhijiang College, May 6th

We respect Mr. Liu's opinions and hereby publish the above "questions" for the study of readers who are concerned about labor issues. Regarding the evaluation of the Quarterly Journal of Labor Problems, we do not completely agree with Mr. Wang's words, but we cannot agree with Mr. Liu's statement that "both are right." The value of the publication is for the publication itself to explain, and we do not want to waste words.

Now we will answer Mr. Liu's questions.

Mr. Liu asked, "What kind of attitude should the laboring masses in semi-colonies take towards their own national capitalists?" The answer is very simple: In the sense of economic struggle, the semi-colonial workers treat their own national capitalists in no way differently from the imperialist factory owners, nor should there be any difference. They are both the objects of the working class struggle, but in the political sense, it is not the case. If the national capitalist class is standing on the true anti-imperialist position, the working class supports the national capitalist class and forms an anti-imperialist alliance. Conversely, if the national bourgeoisie does not oppose imperialism and they become an obstacle to national liberation, then they are also opposed in politics. Thus, anti-imperialism and anti-native capital are mixed into a single object of struggle.

Taking the sentence "The national labor-capital struggle is often more intense than the ordinary labor-capital struggle" in isolation, it can naturally be said that it does not hide anything. However, if we go on to explain that this is why the Shanghai workers can act as the main force of the nation, this kind of flattery clearly comes from the condition that the workers' "resistance to domestic capitalists is relatively mild." This cannot but contain an incorrect meaning, so we believe that our reply to Mr. Wang is still correct. As for Mr. Liu's saying: "According to Mr.'s meaning, the workers are not enough, who is enough? Warlords?" We deeply regret Mr. Liu. Mr. Liu did not read a sentence thoroughly, and then carelessly raised a protest. It is a pity for Mr. Liu. This "extremely insufficient" clearly refers to the author of the article explaining that this is not enough for Shanghai workers to be the main force of the nation because "the national labor-capital struggle is often more intense than the ordinary labor-capital struggle," but Mr. Liu did not see it, which is somewhat close to intentional sophistry. Who is the prisoner of formal logic after all?

For the fifth item of the conclusion, we believe that the words we quoted are correct. Although the result of "recession" is on the one hand the closure of factories and unemployment, on the other hand, it is not what Mr. Liu imagined: "When workers are waiting at home, can a major strike occur?" We especially believe that if Mr. Liu intends to study labor issues, he should pay attention to reality and look at the recent riots in Paris, street fighting in Vienna, and the disturbances of the London hunger marchers. Is the great strike in the United States stimulated by the improvement of capitalism? Or is it the result of economic recession? Even in China, this year is the most profound year of recession. The current labor unrest in China is also unprecedented since the May 30th Movement. Recently, a factory in Shanghai burned down, and the improvement of the industry is also enough to stimulate the labor counterattack, but the performance of this period is mostly limited to economic significance, unlike the resolute battle driven by hunger, which contains a strong political meaning. Mr. Liu can remember well the stimulus of industrial improvement to labor, but he forgot that under the recession, there are more scenes that drive workers into the Paris bloodshed. This is also a pity.

"After the 1905-1907 Russian Revolution, the "temporary decline" of the workers' movement is a fact. On the one hand, it was because Russia entered the era of great reaction at that time, and the political oppression made the fragile Russian labor movement have to temporarily decline. At the same time, it was also because of the division of the Russian Social Democratic Party at that time, which lost strong leadership. Today is no longer the era of 1905-1907, and the old tune cannot be sung again. We don't want to use words here to argue about the current labor situation in China. We want to ask Mr. Liu to look at the current development of facts. Don't just look at the surface, but observe in depth.

In short: The article "A Review and Significance of the Shanghai Workers' Movement" is not only a problem with writing, but also a theoretical error and a distorted explanation, which has a bad influence on general readers. (End)

Spring and Autumn

Records of Lingering Fragrance 184

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

In the current National Government of China, or in the 　 country, or in other countries, a person who serves as Minister of Internal Affairs or an equivalent position always holds a very important political status; however, the Qing Shan that we are discussing here is different. The matters he handles are all trivial and very minor. So, to put it precisely, he is really equivalent to a servant or butler in a wealthy family. His "internal affairs" are actually "palace affairs." And the difference between his position and other ministers is only that he is more often in the palace near the Empress Dowager than others. If, on the right occasion, the Empress Dowager happens to want to use him, she will have him do some miscellaneous tasks nearby; in this way, he can also take the opportunity to curry favor.

No matter how mediocre his talent is, no matter how unimportant his position is, his attire is indeed very exquisite! In this chapter of the book, the main point that the author wants to describe is the attire of these ministers. Their attire is all in accordance with the standard, as neat as a uniform. As usual, Qing Shan also wore a small umbrella-style cap, with a red coral bead on the top of the cap; in the Manchu Qing Dynasty, the red bead was the symbol of a first-rank minister, and it was extremely valuable! There was also a peacock feather trailing behind the cap. When his head swayed, there were often dazzling lights flashing. Of course, he could not use a "double-eyed" feather, because this kind of feather was the most glorious decoration, and it was absolutely forbidden to abuse it without the permission of the court. In the three hundred years of the Qing Dynasty, only three or four people were able to obtain this special reward. One of them was the famous Hefei Li Hongzhang. (29)

Chess 185

— Yizhen

Chess is the most common entertainment in our China. Ordinary people know how to play, what jumping horses, flying elephants, drawing cars, promoting pawns, righteous scholars...

...used very quickly.

The meaning of playing chess is inevitably to kill time and relieve boredom, but it is also a good way to exercise thinking.

I remember once when I returned to my hometown from Shanghai, sitting opposite me was an Englishman. After the car passed Longhua, he took out a beautiful set of chess and strongly invited me to play. He was actually very skilled in this set. He said, "Chinese mahjong and chess are indeed great inventions. This thing is also very popular in our England. When playing chess, thoughts are silent and the spirit is united." The words were well said, and I replied at the time: "Yes, your playing cards are also a great invention!" Both of them laughed.

Originally, chess was a noble toy listed as one of the "qinqi calligraphy and painting". Now, old guns have made a set of fir wood, set up a tripod, and are actually doing business on the side of the road, which is too insulting to the chess pieces.

Chess is a microcosm of life. French Yi Mo Jiamei said in Lu Bai

Collection: "Life is just a set of pitiful chess pieces, painting and night are a chessboard, let him go east and west, and after walking, collect them all in the box."

Supplement to Circular Nouns 186

— Zuichisheng

The other day I read the "Qifeng Louzhu" circular nouns in this publication, which were quite interesting. It is based on two words that are repeatedly chanted, and the explanation of their meaning is very different. However, there are many like this: I will re-record several items as far as I can remember, just to make up for the shortcomings.

(London) The capital of the United States. (Dunlun) The relationship between husband and wife is called Dunlun. This is a term set by former moralists. (Subordinates) Military and political officers call their subordinates subordinates. (Lower body) The private parts of the human body are called lower body. I still remember that in the late Qing Dynasty, a military officer submitted a memorial. There was a sentence in it: "The subordinates are still elite and available." The two words subordinates were reversed and written as "The lower body is still elite and available." It was passed on as a joke for a while. (Water moon) The moon in the water, that is, the so-called mirror flower and water moon, is a metaphor for its illusion. (Moon water) That is, women's menstruation, also known as moon water. (Gold) It is the most cherished thing in the world. (Golden) A color name. (Japan) It is called the hegemon of East Asia and the neighboring country that invaded our Northeast. (Today) Today. (Big boss) An important person who holds the great power of national politics. (Oldest) Boatmen call their headman the oldest. Also, the store manager is commonly called the oldest. (Green stone) A kind of rock. (Shiqing) A pigment name. (Shadou) The name of a bean. (Dou Sha) Made of red beans. There are also two words that are read upside down, and their meanings are still the same and can be used in general. I also remember a few items!

(Official) (Official) (Brother) (Brother) (Introduction) (Introduction) (Shanghai) (On the sea) (Yesterday) (The day before yesterday) (Kangjian) (Health) (Love) (Love) (Law) (Law) (Important) (Important) (Processing) (Management) (Hospitality) (Response) (Meeting) (Communication) (Feelings) (Face) (Affair) (Matter) (Painting) (Drawing) (Lively) (Lively) (Friend) (Friend)

Chapter 28: A Coincidence at the Theater, Infatuation Over a Handkerchief, Earnest Inquiries About Illness, a Misunderstanding Leads to a Letter

Ji-zhi thought about it and felt very uneasy. If he recovered from his illness, how would he answer his brother and sister-in-law's questioning? As he thought, he suddenly changed his mind. He was already living independently and not dependent on his brother and sister-in-law. They might not be able to interfere with his personal actions. If they really asked, he could just say it was his girlfriend's handkerchief, which wouldn't be a problem. Wasn't a girlfriend exactly what an unmarried man should want? With this change of thought, he felt justified. Therefore, he stopped worrying about where the handkerchief had gone. In fact, the handkerchief had not caught the attention of the person inside the gate. Two hours before he regained consciousness, the news had already been passed back to the handkerchief's original owner. It turned out that the play yesterday not only caused Gan Jizhi to catch a cold, but also affected Gui Zhi, who was pregnant, causing her to experience a threatened miscarriage. So, the next morning, Zhao Weng invited Wang, a famous Chinese medicine doctor from Haitien Street, to see her. Doctor Wang usually liked to play chess, and so did Zhao Weng. They were chess friends. After taking the pulse, Dr. Wang chatted with Zhao Weng in the main room. Dr. Wang chuckled and said, "During these times of year, doctors are always busy because people eat the wrong things." Zhao Weng said, "Dr. Wang, you just saw Mr. Gan from across the street. Did he also eat the wrong things?" Dr. Wang said, "Probably. He probably ate too much and caught a cold. Sigh! Young people these days don't care about anything, even when they're on their deathbeds, they still want to be in love." Zhao Weng said, "Are you talking about Mr. Gan?" Dr. Wang said, "Who else? He has such a bad cold, and he still keeps a woman's handkerchief under his pillow." Zhao Weng laughed, "How do you know it's a woman's handkerchief?" (380)

, can be used as filling. (Spoken Dialogue) Dialogue in drama and ballad singing.

Difficult May 188

One-Act Play

Love School (Part 1) 189

— Yin Yiqiu

Characters: Silly Girl (Maiden), Pitiful Worm (Love Doctor), Dozens of Male Students, Dozens of Female Students

(A school classroom setup, with desks, chairs, a teacher's platform, a blackboard, etc.; but instead of maps on the walls, there are many pictures of courtship poses and Western love paintings.)

(The Principal stands solemnly on the platform at the opening.)

Principal: The courtship methods I taught you last time, you must have all tried them out in practice. Now, everyone report on your results!

Student A: Yesterday, I tried the second step of courtship on Miss Zhang, and she already loves me, but she wants me to buy her a diamond ring, which is terrible! Teacher! Where am I going to get a diamond ring?

Principal: That's easy. You say to her like this: "I hate diamond rings the most. Many men have used them to deceive countless women's love; many women have had their chastity ruined and their souls stained by them, Miss Zhang! I don't want to use such dirty things to exchange for your sacred love! You want my heart, and I can dig it out and give it to you immediately, Miss Zhang! I really respect you and love you so much!"

Student A: What if saying that doesn't work?

Principal: Then you implement our school's third step of courtship, use the "bitter tactic" to deal with her, and you'll definitely succeed!

Principal: Oh no! Oh no! You've all reached the second stage of love sickness! Hurry up and consult the love medicine I compiled!

(The students all bend over their desks and flip through books丨a pink book)

Principal: Okay! Class is almost over! Do you have any questions about the study of love?

Student C: Teacher! What exactly is love?

Principal: Love is like a wintergreen tree, always green and never withering; however, sometimes when the weather is too hot, it will also turn scarlet!

Student D: Teacher! What exactly is a woman?

Principal: A woman is like a bottle of fine wine, it smells very fragrant! It tastes very sweet, but if you take two or three sips, you'll get drunk. Student: Teacher! Then what is a man?

Principal: A man is a candle! The more arrogant and stuck-up a woman is, the more you want to love her; if a woman automatically comes to love you first, you will definitely feel it's bland, tasteless, and even annoying. Alas! Men are really candles! Pitiful Worm: Teacher! Are you a man?

Principal: You idiot! Shut your mouth!

At this moment, the bell rings backstage, and the male and female students all leave the stage hand in hand, leaving only the Principal and the Pitiful Worm.

Principal: Look! Everyone else is playing around in pairs, only you, you idiot! You're always dull and stupid, and you still haven't found a lover. Like this, it's a big problem for our school's reputation. All the students who graduate from our school are victorious generals in the battlefield of love, only you, so hopeless!

Okay! I'm giving you three days! If you still haven't found a lover by the fourth day, you're expelled immediately! Expelled immediately! (The Principal leaves the stage in anger)

Pitiful Worm: Boo hoo hoo! (Bursts into tears while lying on the desk) (Silly Girl enters)

Silly Girl: Ah! Why are you crying?

Pitiful Worm: (Hears a woman's voice, looks up in joy) Ah! Miss...Miss...Miss Miss (Kneels down) I...I...I...I...I from my mother's womb, I...I from one year old until now, I...I from coming to this world...from...from...from...from never seen; seen, such a beautiful...beautiful...beauty!

Silly Girl: Yo! Get up quickly (Helps the Pitiful Worm up) I...I...I also from...from...from never seen...seen such a handsome...handsome...handsome man.

(They fall in love at first sight)

Pitiful Worm: I love you!

Silly Girl: I love you too!

Sports News: Far Eastern Games Tennis Draw Set; China vs. Japan in First Round; Shanghai Fundraising for City Sports Ground Already at 2,000 Philippine Pesos in the Philippines 190

(Special dispatch from Manila by this newspaper on the 8th) The draw for the Far Eastern Games men's tennis tournament has been set. In the first round, China will play against Japan, and the Philippines against Java. The winners of the two groups will meet in the final.

(Special dispatch from Manila by this newspaper on the 8th) Fundraising for the Shanghai City Sports Ground in the Philippines has already reached 2,000 Philippine pesos, with hopes of reaching 10,000 Philippine pesos.

Far Eastern Games to Open on Schedule; Chinese Team Arrives in the Philippines; Enthusiastic Welcome by Overseas Chinese; Lands Amidst Music; Immediately Parades Around the City; Practice Begins Today; However, the Weather Is Too Hot, and the Chinese Athletes Are Not Accustomed To It 191

(Central News Agency dispatch from Manila on the 8th) The Chinese team for the Far Eastern Games arrived safely and on schedule, reaching the Philippines at 8:30 AM on the 8th. Over ten thousand overseas Chinese and a band gave an enthusiastic welcome at the pier. After the ship docked, physical and luggage inspections were carried out. Representatives of the Philippine Sports Association and Mr. Kuang Guanglin, the Chinese Consul-General in the Philippines, boarded the ship to welcome them. Over ten female overseas Chinese presented flowers. At 11:00 AM, the team, led by Chief Representative Wang Zhengting, disembarked and rode in over twenty cars, parading around the city, visiting La Salle University and the National Women's University for accommodation. They rested in the afternoon and began practice on the 9th. Athletes from all countries have arrived in the Philippines. The Games are scheduled to open on the 12th. However, the weather is too hot, and the Chinese athletes are not accustomed to it.

(Special dispatch from a Telecommunications Agency correspondent in Manila on the 8th) The Chinese delegation to the Far Eastern Games, led by Chief Representative Wang Zhengting, representatives Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, and others, totaling 156 people, arrived in Manila this morning at 9:30 AM on the President McKinley. Thousands of officials from the Philippine Sports Association and overseas Chinese in Manila, holding Qing Tian Bai Ri flags, gave them a warm welcome at the pier. The Philippine Sports Association sent a band, the same as they did to welcome the Japanese athletes the day before. After the athletes disembarked amidst the music, they rode in dozens of cars to visit the Governor's Mansion, the Congress, and the City Hall to pay their respects. Then, they went to their dormitories to rest.

(Dispatch from the Manila correspondent of the Japan United Press on the 7th) The Chinese team will arrive in Manila at 8:00 AM on the 8th. The athletes are full of energy. When the ship arrives at the pier, representatives of the Philippine Sports Association, athlete representatives, and many overseas Chinese residing in the Philippines will welcome them. After the team disembarks, they will ride in dozens of cars, led by a military band playing marches, through the city. The overseas Chinese lining both sides of the road will see the athletes raising the national flag and shouting "Long live the Republic of China." The citizens of Manila will also applaud to express their sympathy. The team will visit various agencies such as the Philippine Sports Association, the Mayor's residence, and the Philippine Governor's Mansion, receiving welcome from all sides. Then, they will enter the dormitories.

(Dispatch from the Manila correspondent of the Japan United Press on the 8th) The Chinese team attending the Far Eastern Games arrived in the Philippines at 8:30 AM on the 8th and received a warm welcome from the overseas Chinese. Team leader Wang Zhengting made the following remarks after arriving in port: "This time, our team is more organized than before, and we should be able to achieve considerable results in this tournament, especially in football and volleyball."

Smooth Sailing Arrival in the Philippines; Manila Customs Conducts Strict Luggage Inspection; Detailed Report of the Chinese Team's Arrival in the Philippines from Hong Kong 192

(Special dispatch from Manila by this newspaper on the 8th) Our delegation arrived in Hong Kong at 10:30 AM on Sunday (the 6th). Before the ship docked in Kowloon, a special small boat came to greet us. Hong Kong Sports Association officials, Li Huitang, and Yang Xiuqiong all came to welcome us. At 1:00 PM, a banquet was held at the South China Athletic Association. Wang Zhengting gave a speech. In the afternoon, the athletes practiced at the South China Athletic Association's field. Xu Xinji and Qiu Feihai played doubles against Lin Wangsu and Jiang Daozhang. The baseball team played a friendly match against the crew of the President McKinley and won 4-3.

The ship set sail from Hong Kong at 7:00 PM. A total of 80 people boarded the ship in Hong Kong: 25 Guangdong athletes and 55 Hong Kong athletes. The delegation consisted of 30 officials, including Yang Xiuqiong's mother, 18 baseball players, 12 basketball players, 17 football players, 3 rifle shooters, and Dai Changling, who did not leave Shanghai due to personal reasons but will be joined by Li Baojun and Shu Hong later. There are 11 swimmers, including 2 water polo players, who will travel to the Philippines on the Coolidge. Chen Zhenxing is ill in Hong Kong and hopes to come to the Philippines on the Coolidge. There are 4 female swimmers, 3 male tennis players, Lin Wangsu, who although accompanied to the Philippines, suffers from discomfort since the sea voyage from Singapore to Hong Kong, fearing affecting performance, 4 female tennis players, 29 track and field athletes, 18 volleyball players, and 15 female volleyball players, for a total of 133 athletes.

The Guangdong side proposed to send an additional six volleyball players, but it was not approved by the National Sports Association. As a result of the discussion, these six will no longer participate but will be allowed to visit the Philippines. In the formal line-up, the Guangdong side will have four representatives participating.

On Monday evening, Chief Representative Wang Zhengting gave a speech on the McKinley about China's road to sports, attended by many listeners. Western passengers and crew members were all in attendance.

On the way to Manila, the sea was calm and there were no cases of seasickness. We arrived in Manila at 10:30 AM this morning. The dock was greeted by 8,000 people. The entire delegation drove around the city in cars. The male athletes were housed at La Salle University, and the female athletes were housed at the Women's College of the University of the Philippines. Wang Zhengting and his wife stayed at the residence of Consul General Kuang Guanglin. Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, Shi Zhaokang, and others stayed at Manila hotels, which were extremely crowded.

The sports field is still under construction, with work being done day and night. The athletes from Annam have not yet arrived. Manila Customs is conducting strict luggage inspections. Even Wang Zhengting's suitcase was inspected.

Wang Zhengting delivered a speech expressing his sincerity to the Philippines and thanking them for their warm welcome. Over 7,000 overseas Chinese came to express their condolences today.

The National Construction Scholarship Committee Regulations, Totaling 15 Articles, Were Promulgated by the National Government Yesterday 203

(Dispatch from Nanjing on the 8th) The National Government promulgated 15 articles of the National Construction Scholarship Committee Regulations by decree on the 8th. The content is that the committee is jointly established by the Examination Yuan and the Ministry of Education, with three presidents, one chairman, one vice-chairman, and several committee members. The scope of the scholarship is limited to dissertations, academic writings, and inventions. The scholarship fund is allocated by the government and assisted by private groups. A fund management committee is established separately to manage the funds, and the 11 articles of the management committee regulations are also promulgated.

Local: Municipal Education Bureau Establishes a Committee for Compiling Teaching Progress Schedules for All Subjects 209

Japanese Ministry of Education Invites Zhou Shang to Attend Health Education Conference 212

Discussing School Health Issues

Zhou Ding Expected to Return to Shanghai in Mid-May

The Shanghai Municipal Education and Health Bureaus previously sent Zhou Shang, a specialist from the Education Bureau, to Japan to investigate health education. He has been there for over a month and has reportedly collected a considerable amount of material and visited relevant health education institutions. From April 30th to May 3rd, the Japanese Ministry of Education held a conference of school health experts and specifically invited Zhou to attend for joint research. Huang Linsheng, supervisor of Chinese students in Japan, and Lin Dingping, section chief, introduced Wu Shishou of the Imperial University's Medical Department to provide translation. The issues discussed at the conference included (1) the duties of school nurses, (2) school meals, (3) health training and guidance, (4) sports medical guidance, and (5) health issues for faculty and staff, totaling over thirty categories. It is now expected that Zhou will return to Shanghai in mid-May to report on his findings.

The China Vocational Education Society's Annual Meeting to Be Held in Jiangxi 214

Cheng Bailu, Director of the Jiangxi Education Department, Serves as Preparation Director

The China Vocational Education Society holds an annual meeting of members once a year. Since 1929, the National Vocational Education Conference has also been resolved to be held at the same time as the Society's annual meeting. It is now known that this year's conference is scheduled to be held in Nanchang, Jiangxi, starting on July 13th. The venue will be the auditorium of the Jiangxi Education Department. Cheng Bailu, Director of the Jiangxi Provincial Education Department, has been appointed as the preparation director, and Wang Boqiu, Zhou Pinggeng, Cheng Ganhou, and Xiong Zhuoru have been appointed as preparation committee members. The Society has publicly appointed Yang Changqing, Chiang Song Meiling, Xiong Tianyi, Ding Chaowu, Gong Bocun, and Gu Shusen as the presidium. The Society has reported to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping and has requested approval from the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications to reduce transportation costs for members attending the conference. Members attending the conference and representatives of vocational education institutions must report their names, ages, genders, and starting and ending stations to the Society before May 30th in order to be registered and submitted to the Ministry for verification and issuance of discounted travel certificates. The agenda for this year's conference, as determined by the preparatory committee, is to focus on national revitalization, with vocational curricula, rural improvement, vocational guidance, and supplementary education as the scope. All members have been notified, and education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities have been invited to send representatives to attend.
